google_ad_request_done(google_ads)
{




window['google_ads']
=
google_ads;




if(google_ads.length
!=
0)
{








apply_ad_config(google_ads.length);









render_ads(true,
window['ad_config_top']);









if(window['backfillParam'])
{












window['backfillParam']['pl_rnum']
=
google_ads.length;












window['backfillParam']['pl_time']
=
Date.now()
-
afc_ad_start_time;








}




}
}

function
apply_ad_config(num)
{
window['ad_config_top']
=
Math.min(2,
num);
window['ad_config_bot']
=
Math.min(2,
num);
}

google_ad_client
=
'ca-aj-cat';
google_ad_channel
=
'cx_ask_wiki,ad_dirN';
google_ad_output
=
'js';
google_max_num_ads
=
'4';
google_ad_type
=
'text';

=
'';

'';
google_language
=
'';
google_country
=
'';
google_encoding
=
'utf8';

=

google_kw
=
'';
google_kw_type
=
'broad';


var
backfillParam
=
{




pl_rqnum
:
google_max_num_ads,




pl_hints
:
google_hints,




pl_rp
:
"false",




pl_kw
:
google_kw,




pl_cl
:
google_ad_client,

:
google_ad_channel,

:
"#FDFEEE",




pl_type
:
"afc",




pl_clksp
:
"none"};

var
word_arr
;

var
word_arr_len
;


function
highlightQuery(input_str)
{

var
queryTokenArray
=
"bj&#38;#246;rk,";


var
tok_arr
=
queryTokenArray.split(",");

for(tok_arr_idx=0;
tok_arr_idx
<
tok_arr.length-1;
tok_arr_idx
++)
{

if(isCombinationWord(tok_arr[tok_arr_idx])){
word_arr
=
tok_arr[tok_arr_idx].split("-");
word_arr_len
=
word_arr.length;
first_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(word_arr[0],0);

if(first_pos
!=-1)
{
input_str
=
highlightCombinationWords(input_str,first_pos);
}
}
else
{
first_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(tok_arr[tok_arr_idx],0);
if(first_pos
!=
-1
&&
tok_arr[tok_arr_idx].length
>
0)
{
input_str
=
highlightSimpleWords(input_str,tok_arr[tok_arr_idx],first_pos);
}
}
}
return
input_str;
}

function
isCombinationWord(word){
if(word.indexOf("-")
!=
-1){
return
true;
}
else
{
return
false;
}
}


function
isAlpha(ch)
{
if
(ch
!=
null
&&
ch.match(/^[a-zA-Z0-9]+$/)){
return
true;
}
return
false;
}

function
isQueryinInput(firstindex,
input_str,
j){
for(i=firstindex;
i<
input_str.length
;
++i)
{
var
currindex
=
i;

if(!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(i)))
{
if(firstindex
==
currindex)

{
firstindex++;
}
else
{
if(word_arr[j]
!=
input_str.substring(firstindex,currindex).toLowerCase())
return
-1;
if
(j
==
word_arr_len-1)
return
currindex;
else
return
isQueryinInput(currindex+1,input_str,++j);
}
}
}

if(j
<
word_arr_len)
{
if(word_arr[j]
!=
input_str.substring(firstindex,currindex+1).toLowerCase())
return
-1;
}

return
(currindex
+
1)
;
}


function

highlightCombinationWords(input_str,first_pos)
{
exactmatch
=
isQueryinInput(first_pos+word_arr[0].length,input_str,1)
;
if(exactmatch
!=-1
)

{
bold_str
=
"<b>"
+
input_str.substring(first_pos,exactmatch)
+
"</b>";
input_str
=
input_str.substring(0,first_pos)
+
bold_str
+
input_str.substring(exactmatch);
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(word_arr[0],exactmatch+7);
while(next_pos
!=
-1)
{
return
highlightCombinationWords(input_str,next_pos);
}
}
return
input_str;
}


function

highlightSimpleWords(input_str,token,
first_pos)
{
var
end_pos
=
first_pos
+
token.length;
if(!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(end_pos))
&&
!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(first_pos-1))){
bold_str
=
"<b>"
+
input_str.substring(first_pos,end_pos)
+
"</b>";
input_str
=
input_str.substring(0,first_pos)
+
bold_str
+
input_str.substring(end_pos);
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(token,end_pos+7);
}
else
{
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(token,end_pos);
}

while(next_pos
!=
-1)
{
return
highlightSimpleWords(input_str,token,next_pos);
}
return
input_str;
}</script>

musical

is

in

and
she
has
achieved
recognition
in
<a
href="/wiki/Alternative_rock?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Alternative

rock</a>,
<a

music</a>,
<a

onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Classical
music">classical</a>,
and
<a

title="Avant-garde

href="#cite_note-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Three
of
Bj&ouml;rk's
1990s
singles
charted
in
the
<a
href="/wiki/UK_Singles_Chart?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="UK
Singles
Chart">UK
Top
10</a>
(&quot;<a
href="/wiki/It%27s_Oh_So_Quiet?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="It's
Oh
So
Quiet">It's
Oh
So
Quiet</a>&quot;
reached
number
4,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Army_of_Me_(Bj%C3%B6rk_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Army
of
Me
(Bj&ouml;rk
song)">Army
of
Me</a>&quot;
number
10,
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Hyperballad?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hyperballad">Hyperballad</a>&quot;
number
8).<sup
id="cite_ref-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup>
Her
record
label,
<a
href="/wiki/One_Little_Indian_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="One
Little
Indian
Records">One
Little
Indian</a>,
reported
that
by
2003,
she
had
sold
more
than
15
million
albums
worldwide.<sup
id="cite_ref-4"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup>
She
has
won
four
<a
href="/wiki/BRIT_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="BRIT
Awards"
class="mw-redirect">BRIT
Awards</a>,
four
<a
href="/wiki/MTV_Video_Music_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="MTV
Video
Music
Awards"
class="mw-redirect">MTV
Video
Music
Awards</a>,
one
<a
href="/wiki/MOJO_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="MOJO
Awards">MOJO
Award</a>,
three
<a
href="/wiki/UK_Music_Video_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="UK
Music
Video
Awards">UK
Music
Video
Awards</a>,
and,
in
2010,
the
<a
href="/wiki/Polar_Music_Prize?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Polar
Music
Prize">Polar
Music
Prize</a>
from
the
<a
href="/wiki/Royal_Swedish_Academy_of_Music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Royal
Swedish
Academy
of
Music">Royal
Swedish
Academy
of
Music</a>
in
recognition
of
her
&quot;deeply
personal
music
and
lyrics,
her
precise
arrangements
and
her
unique
voice.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-polarmusicprize.org_5-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-polarmusicprize.org-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Bj&ouml;rk
has
also
been
nominated
for
14
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Award?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Award">Grammy
Awards</a>
(plus
two
for
art
direction
on
her
album
sleeves,
done
by
others),
one
<a
href="/wiki/Academy_Award?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Academy
Award"
class="mw-redirect">Academy
Award</a>,
and
two
<a
href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Golden
Globe
Award">Golden
Globe
Awards</a>.
She
won
the
<a
href="/wiki/Best_Actress_Award_(Cannes_Film_Festival)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Best
Actress
Award
(Cannes
Film
Festival)">Best
Actress
Award</a>
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/2000_Cannes_Film_Festival?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="2000
Cannes
Film
Festival">2000
Cannes
Film
Festival</a>
for
her
performance
in
<i><a
href="/wiki/Dancer_in_the_Dark?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Dancer
in
the
Dark">Dancer
in
the
Dark</a></i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-festival-cannes.com_6-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-festival-cannes.com-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup>
She
was
ranked
twenty-ninth
in
<a
href="/wiki/VH1?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="VH1">VH1</a>'s
&quot;The
100
Greatest
Women
in
Music&quot;,<sup
id="cite_ref-7"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup>
eighth
in
<a
href="/wiki/MTV?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="MTV">MTV</a>'s
&quot;22
Greatest
Voices
in
Music&quot;,<sup
id="cite_ref-MTV_voices_8-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-MTV_voices-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
sixtieth
in
<i><a
href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rolling
Stone">Rolling
Stone</a></i><span
style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s
&quot;100
Greatest
Singers
of
All
Time&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-Rolling_Stone_voices_9-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Rolling_Stone_voices-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Life_and_career">Life
and
career</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Bj%C3%B6rk&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1"
title="Edit
section:
Life
and
career">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="1965.E2.80.9386:_Early_life_and_career_beginnings">1965–86:
Early
life
and
career
beginnings</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Bj%C3%B6rk&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2"
title="Edit
section:
1965–86:
Early
life
and
career
beginnings">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<div
class="thumb
tright">









<div
class="thumbinner"
style="width:232px;">









<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Reykjavik_rooftops.jpg"
target="_blank"
class="image"><img
alt=""
src="http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Reykjavik_rooftops.jpg/230px-Reykjavik_rooftops.jpg"
width="230"
height="173"
class="thumbimage"
srcset="http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Reykjavik_rooftops.jpg/345px-Reykjavik_rooftops.jpg
1.5x,
http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Reykjavik_rooftops.jpg/460px-Reykjavik_rooftops.jpg
2x"
/></a>










<div
class="thumbcaption">











<div
class="magnify">











<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Reykjavik_rooftops.jpg"
target="_blank"
class="internal"
title="Enlarge"><img
src="http://sp.ask.com/sh/i/wiki/magnify-clip.png"
width="15"
height="11"
alt=""
/></a>










</div>
The
city
of











<a
href="/wiki/Reykjav%C3%ADk?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Reykjav&iacute;k">Reykjav&iacute;k</a>,
Iceland,
where
Bj&ouml;rk
was
born
and
raised









</div>









</div>








</div>








<p>Bj&ouml;rk
was
born
on
November
21,
1965
in
<a
href="/wiki/Reykjav%C3%ADk?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Reykjav&iacute;k">Reykjav&iacute;k,
Iceland</a>,
where
she
grew
up.
Her
mother
is
activist
Hildur
R&uacute;na
Hauksd&oacute;ttir,
who
protested
against
the
controversial
development
of
Iceland's
<a
href="/wiki/K%C3%A1rahnj%C3%BAkar_Hydropower_Plant?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="K&aacute;rahnj&uacute;kar
Hydropower
Plant">K&aacute;rahnj&uacute;kar
Hydropower
Plant</a>,<sup
id="cite_ref-10"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
her
father
is
<a
href="/wiki/Gu%C3%B0mundur_Gunnarsson?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Gu&eth;mundur
Gunnarsson">Gu&eth;mundur
Gunnarsson</a>,
a
union
leader
and
electrician.
They
divorced
when
Bj&ouml;rk
was
born
and
she
moved
on
with
her
mother
in
a
<a
href="/wiki/Hippie?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hippie">hippie</a>
<a
href="/wiki/Commune?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Commune">commune</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-swipnetbio_11-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-swipnetbio-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-secrethistory_12-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-secrethistory-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup>
Her
stepfather
is
S&aelig;var
&Aacute;rnason,
a
former
guitarist
in
a
band
called
Pops.<sup
id="cite_ref-secrethistory_12-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-secrethistory-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup>
At
six,
Bj&ouml;rk
enrolled
at
Reykjav&iacute;k
school
Barnam&uacute;s&iacute;ksk&oacute;li,
where
she
studied
<a
href="/wiki/Piano?qsrc=3044#History_and_musical_performance"
title="Piano">classical
piano</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Flute?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Flute">flute</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-saga_13-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-saga-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup>
After
a
school
recital
in
which
Bj&ouml;rk
sang
<a
href="/wiki/Tina_Charles_(singer)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tina
Charles
(singer)">Tina
Charles</a>
1976
hit
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/I_Love_to_Love_(But_My_Baby_Loves_to_Dance)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="I
Love
to
Love
(But
My
Baby
Loves
to
Dance)">I
Love
to
Love</a>&quot;,
her
teachers
sent
a
recording
of
her
singing
the
song
to
the
<a
href="/wiki/R%C3%A1s_1?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="R&aacute;s
1">R&Uacute;V
radio
station</a>
–
then,
Iceland's
only
radio
station.
The
recording
was
nationally
broadcast
and,
after
hearing
it,
a
representative
of
the
<a
href="/wiki/F%C3%A1lkinn?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="F&aacute;lkinn">F&aacute;lkinn
record
label</a>
offered
Bj&ouml;rk
a
recording
contract.
Her
selt-titled
d&eacute;but,
<a
href="/wiki/Bj%C3%B6rk_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bj&ouml;rk
(album)"><i>Bj&ouml;rk</i></a>
was
recorded
and
released
in
December
1977.
The
album
went
<a
href="/wiki/Music_recording_sales_certification?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Music
recording
sales
certification">platinum</a>
in
Iceland
but
the
young
singer
turned
down
the
offer
of
doing
a
second
album.<sup
id="cite_ref-secrethistory_12-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-secrethistory-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-saga_13-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-saga-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>During
her
teens,
after
the
diffusion
of
<a
href="/wiki/Punk_rock?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Punk
rock">punk
rock</a>
music
in
Iceland
she
formed
the
<a
href="/wiki/All-female_band?qsrc=3044#1970s"
title="All-female
band">all-girl
punk
band</a>
Spit
and
Snot.
A
year
later,
in
1980,
she
formed
a
<a
href="/wiki/Jazz_fusion?qsrc=3044#1970s"
title="Jazz
fusion">jazz
fusion</a>
group
called
Exodus
and
collaborated
in
another
group
called
JAM80.
During
the
same
year
she
also
graduated
from
music
school.<sup
id="cite_ref-saga_13-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-saga-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
1982,
she
and
<a
href="/wiki/Bassist?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bassist">bassist</a>
Jakob
Magn&uacute;sson
formed
another
group,
<a
href="/wiki/Tappi_T%C3%ADkarrass?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tappi
T&iacute;karrass">Tappi
T&iacute;karrass</a>
(&quot;Cork
the
Bitch's
Ass
<small>[<i><a
href="/wiki/Sic?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sic">sic</a></i>]</small>&quot;
in
<a
href="/wiki/Icelandic_language?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Icelandic
language">Icelandic</a>),
and
released
<a
href="/wiki/Extended_play?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Extended
play">EP</a>
<i><a
href="/wiki/B%C3%ADti%C3%B0_Fast_%C3%AD_V%C3%ADti%C3%B0?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="B&iacute;ti&eth;
Fast
&iacute;
V&iacute;ti&eth;">B&iacute;ti&eth;
Fast
&iacute;
V&iacute;ti&eth;</a></i>
(&quot;Bite
Hard
Into
Hell&quot;
in
Icelandic),
in
August
1982.
Their
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Miranda_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Miranda
(album)">Miranda</a></i>
was
released
in
December
1983.
The
group
was
featured
in
the
documentary
<i><a
href="/wiki/Rokk_%C3%AD_Reykjav%C3%ADk?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rokk
&iacute;
Reykjav&iacute;k">Rokk
&iacute;
Reykjav&iacute;k</a></i>,
with
Bj&ouml;rk
particularly
being
featured
on
the
cover
of
the
VHS
release.<sup
id="cite_ref-saga_13-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-saga-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-14"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup>
It
was
around
this
time
that
the
singer
got
to
meet
with
guitarist
&THORN;&oacute;r
Eldon
and
<a
href="/wiki/Surrealism?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Surrealism">surrealist</a>
group
Medusa,
which
also
included
poet
<a
href="/wiki/Sj%C3%B3n?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sj&oacute;n">Sj&oacute;n</a>,
with
whom
she
started
a
life-long
collaboration
and
formed
a
small
group
called
Rokka
Rokka
Drum.<sup
id="cite_ref-15"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
singer
appeared
as
a
featured
artist
on
&quot;Afi&quot;,
a
track
from
Bj&ouml;rgvin
G&iacute;slason
1983
record
<i>&Ouml;rugglega</i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-secrethistory_12-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-secrethistory-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Due
to
the
imminent
discontinuance
of
radio
show
<i>&Aacute;fangar</i>,
two
radio
personalities,
&Aacute;smundur
J&oacute;nsson
and
Gu&eth;ni
R&uacute;nar,
called
out
to
musicians
to
play
on
a
last
live
radio
show.
Bj&ouml;rk
joined
with
Einar
Melax
(from
the
group
Fan
Houtens
K&oacute;k&oacute;),
<a
href="/wiki/Einar_%C3%96rn_Benediktsson?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Einar
&Ouml;rn
Benediktsson">Einar
&Ouml;rn
Benediktsson</a>
(from
Purrkur
Pillnikk),
<a
href="/wiki/Gu%C3%B0laugur_Kristinn_%C3%93ttarsson?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Gu&eth;laugur
Kristinn
&Oacute;ttarsson">Gu&eth;laugur
Kristinn
&Oacute;ttarsson</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Sigtryggur_Baldursson?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sigtryggur
Baldursson">Sigtryggur
Baldursson</a>
(from
&THORN;eyr),
and
Birgir
Mogensen
(from
Spilaf&iacute;fl)
to
perform
on
the
concert.<sup
id="cite_ref-kuklgunni_16-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-kuklgunni-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
group
developed
a
<a
href="/wiki/Goth_rock?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Goth
rock"
class="mw-redirect">goth
rock</a>
sound.
It
was
during
this
experience
that
Bj&ouml;rk
began
to
develop
her
vocalisation
–
punctuated
by
howls
and
shrieks.<sup
id="cite_ref-saga_13-4"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-saga-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
project
performed
as
Gott
kv&ouml;ld
during
the
concert
but
later
decided
to
keep
playing
together
as
a
group
and
they
used
the
name
<span
lang="is"
xml:lang="is"><a
href="/wiki/Kukl_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Kukl
(band)">Kukl</a></span>
(&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Witchcraft?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Witchcraft">Sorcery</a>&quot;
in
Icelandic).<sup
id="cite_ref-kuklgunni_16-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-kuklgunni-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup>
They
started
recording
at
a
studio
thanks
to
Bj&ouml;rk's
acquaintance
with
the
studio
owner
and
released
their
first
single
in
1983.<sup
id="cite_ref-kuklgunni_16-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-kuklgunni-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup>
Their
first
big
performance
was
at
a
festival
in
Iceland
which
was
headlined
by
English
<a
href="/wiki/Anarchism?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Anarchism">anarchist</a>
punk
band
<a
href="/wiki/Crass?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Crass">Crass</a>,
whose
record
label,
<a
href="/wiki/Crass_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Crass
Records">Crass
Records</a>
offered
the
band
a
record
deal.
<i>The
Eye</i>
was
released
in
1984
and
was
followed
by
a
two-month
tour
in
Europe,
which
also
included
a
performance
at
<a
href="/wiki/Roskilde_Festival?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Roskilde
Festival">Roskilde
Festival</a>
in
<a
href="/wiki/Denmark?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Denmark">Denmark</a>,
making
Kukl
the
first
Icelandic
band
to
play
at
the
festival.<sup
id="cite_ref-swipnetbio_11-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-swipnetbio-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-kuklgunni_16-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-kuklgunni-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup>
During
this
period
Bj&ouml;rk
published
a
handcoloured
book
of
poems
to
sustain
the
cost
of
her
rent.
<i><a
href="/wiki/Um_%C3%9Arnat_fr%C3%A1_Bj%C3%B6rk?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Um
&Uacute;rnat
fr&aacute;
Bj&ouml;rk">Um
&Uacute;rnat
fr&aacute;
Bj&ouml;rk</a></i>
was
distributed
in
1984.<sup
id="cite_ref-saga_13-5"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-saga-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
1985,
the
singer
found
out
she
was
expecting
a
child
from
Eldon,
but
continued
touring
with
Kukl.<sup
id="cite_ref-saga_13-6"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-saga-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup>
Their
second
album,
called
<i>Holidays
in
Europe</i>
came
out
in
1986,
but
after
some
months
the
band
would
eventually
split
up
due
to
personal
squabbles,
with
Bj&ouml;rk
keeping
a
collaboration
with
&Oacute;ttarsson,
which
was
named
<a
href="/wiki/The_Elgar_Sisters?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Elgar
Sisters">The
Elgar
Sisters</a>.
Some
of
the
songs
they
recorded
would
end
up
as
B-sides
to
Bj&ouml;rk
solo
singles.<sup
id="cite_ref-saga_13-7"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-saga-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-part25_17-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-part25-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="1986.E2.80.9392:_The_Sugarcubes">1986–92:
The
Sugarcubes</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a

Bj&ouml;rk
performing
in
Japan
with











<a
href="/wiki/The_Sugarcubes?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Sugarcubes">the
Sugarcubes</a>









</div>









</div>








</div>








<p>On
June
8,
1986,
Bj&ouml;rk
gave
birth
to
a
baby
boy
called
Sindri
Eldon
Th&oacute;rsson.<sup
id="cite_ref-saga_13-8"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-saga-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup>
She
married
&THORN;&oacute;r
Eldon
and
moved
out
with
him.
Soon
after
Sindri
was
born,
Bj&ouml;rk
got
her
first
acting
role
on
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Juniper_Tree_(film)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Juniper
Tree
(film)">The
Juniper
Tree</a></i>,
a
film
directed
by
<a
href="/wiki/Nietzchka_Keene?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Nietzchka
Keene">Nietzchka
Keene</a>,
playing
the
role
of
Margit.<sup
id="cite_ref-saga_13-9"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-saga-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup>
That
summer,
former
band
member
Einar
&Ouml;rn
and
Eldon
formed
the
arts
collective
<i><a
href="/wiki/Bad_Taste_(record_label)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bad
Taste
(record
label)">Smekkleysa</a></i>
(&quot;Bad
Taste&quot;
in
Icelandic),
created
with
the
intention
of
being
both
a
record
label
and
book
publishing
company.<sup
id="cite_ref-saga_13-10"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-saga-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-part25_17-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-part25-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup>
Various
friends,
namely
Melax
and
Sigtryggur
from
the
Kukl,
along
with
<a
href="/wiki/Bragi_%C3%93lafsson?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bragi
&Oacute;lafsson">Bragi
&Oacute;lafsson</a>
and
Fri&eth;rik
Erlingson
from
Purrkur
Pillnikk,
joined
the
group
and
a
band
coalesced
in
the
collective
solely
to
make
money.<sup
id="cite_ref-part25_17-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-part25-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup>
They
were
initially
called
&THORN;ukl,
but
they
were
advertised
as
Kukl
(the
name
of
the
previous
band).
At
a
later
concert
supporting
Icelandic
band
Stu&eth;menn
(managed
by
Einar
&Ouml;rn)
they
addressed
themselves
as
<a
href="/wiki/The_Sugarcubes?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Sugarcubes">Sykurmolarnir</a>
(&quot;The
Sugarcubes&quot;
in
Icelandic).
To
fund
the
release
of
their
first
double
A-side
single
&quot;Einn
mol'&aacute;
mann&quot;,
which
contained
the
songs
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Birthday_(The_Sugarcubes_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Birthday
(The
Sugarcubes
song)">Amm&aelig;li</a>&quot;
(&quot;Birthday&quot;)
and
&quot;K&ouml;ttur&quot;
(&quot;Cat&quot;),
Smekkleysa
printed
a
<a
href="/wiki/Postcard?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Postcard">postcard</a>
bearing
the
image
of
<a
href="/wiki/Mikhail_Gorbachev?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mikhail
Gorbachev">Mikhail
Gorbachev</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Ronald_Reagan?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ronald
Reagan">Ronald
Reagan</a>
during
the
<a
href="/wiki/Reykjav%C3%ADk_Summit?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Reykjav&iacute;k
Summit">Reykjav&iacute;k
Summit</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-saga_13-11"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-saga-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-part25_17-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-part25-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
single
was
released
on
November
21,
1986,
Bj&ouml;rk's
21st
birthday.<sup
id="cite_ref-part25_17-4"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-part25-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup>
At
the
end
of
that
year,
the
band
was
signed
by
<a
href="/wiki/One_Little_Indian?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="One
Little
Indian"
class="mw-redirect">One
Little
Indian</a>,
a
new
label
set
up
by
Derek
Birkett,
the
former
bass
player
of
<a
href="/wiki/Flux_of_Pink_Indians?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Flux
of
Pink
Indians">Flux
of
Pink
Indians</a>,
but
soon
after
Erlingson
decided
to
leave
the
band.<sup
id="cite_ref-part25_17-5"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-part25-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup>
Their
first
English
single,
&quot;Birthday&quot;,
was
released
in
the
<a
href="/wiki/United_Kingdom?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="United
Kingdom">UK</a>
on
August
17,
1987;
a
week
later,
it
was
declared
single
of
the
week
by
<i><a
href="/wiki/Melody_Maker?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Melody
Maker">Melody
Maker</a></i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-part25_17-6"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-part25-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
Sugarcubes
also
signed
a
distribution
deal
with
<a
href="/wiki/Elektra_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Elektra
Records">Elektra
Records</a>
in
the
United
States
turning
down
a
number
of
record
deal
offers
from
around
the
world
and
recorded
their
first
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Life%27s_Too_Good?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Life's
Too
Good">Life's
Too
Good</a></i>,
which
was
released
in
1988.<sup
id="cite_ref-part27_18-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-part27-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup>
After
the
release
of
the
album,
Margr&eacute;t
&quot;Magga&quot;
&Ouml;rn&oacute;lfsd&oacute;ttir,
Eldon's
new
girlfriend
(he
and
Bj&ouml;rk
had
divorced
soon
after
the
birth
of
their
child
despite
being
in
the
same
group<sup
id="cite_ref-saga_13-12"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-saga-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup>),
replaced
Einst
Melax
as
the
band
<a
href="/wiki/Keyboardist?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Keyboardist">keyboardist</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-part27_18-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-part27-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
album
went
on
to
sell
more
than
one
million
copies
worldwide.<sup
id="cite_ref-part27_18-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-part27-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup>
Bj&ouml;rk
contributed
as
a
background
vocalist
on
1987
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Loftmynd?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Loftmynd">Loftmynd</a></i>
by
<a
href="/wiki/Megas?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Megas">Megas</a>,
for
whom
she
provided
background
vocals
also
on
his
subsequent
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/H%C3%B6fu%C3%B0lausnir?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="H&ouml;fu&eth;lausnir">H&ouml;fu&eth;lausnir</a></i>
(1988)
and
<i><a
href="/wiki/H%C3%A6ttuleg_hlj%C3%B3msveit_%26_gl%C3%A6pakvendi%C3%B0_Stella?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="H&aelig;ttuleg
hlj&oacute;msveit
&amp;
gl&aelig;pakvendi&eth;
Stella">H&aelig;ttuleg
hlj&oacute;msveit
&amp;
gl&aelig;pakvendi&eth;
Stella</a></i>
(1990).<sup
id="cite_ref-secrethistory_12-4"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-secrethistory-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
the
last
quarter
of
1988,
The
Sugarcubes
toured
<a
href="/wiki/North_America?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="North
America">North
America</a>
to
positive
reception.<sup
id="cite_ref-part27_18-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-part27-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
September,
the
band
played
at
<a
href="/wiki/The_Ritz_(rock_club)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Ritz
(rock
club)">The
Ritz</a>
in
<a
href="/wiki/New_York_City?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="New
York
City">New
York</a>,
a
concert
attended
by
<a
href="/wiki/David_Bowie?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="David
Bowie">David
Bowie</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Iggy_Pop?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Iggy
Pop">Iggy
Pop</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-part27_18-4"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-part27-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup>
On
October
15,
the
band
appeared
on
<i><a
href="/wiki/Saturday_Night_Live?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Saturday
Night
Live">Saturday
Night
Live</a></i>.
Bj&ouml;rk
alone
contributed
with
a
rendition
of
the
<a
href="/wiki/Christmas?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Christmas">christmas</a>
classic
&quot;J&oacute;lak&ouml;tturinn&quot;
(&quot;The
Christmas
Cat&quot;)
on
the
compilation
<i>Hvitt
Er
&Iacute;
Borg
Og
B&aelig;In</i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-secrethistory_12-5"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-secrethistory-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
band's
second
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Here_Today,_Tomorrow_Next_Week!?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Here
Today,
Tomorrow
Next
Week!">Here
Today,
Tomorrow
Next
Week!</a></i>
saw
release
on
October
1989.<sup
id="cite_ref-part27_18-5"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-part27-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup>
Contrary
to
their
debut
album,
it
was
not
well
received
by
critics.
Due
to
negative
backlash
regarding
Einar
&Ouml;rn
by
music
critics,<sup
id="cite_ref-secrethistory_12-6"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-secrethistory-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-part27_18-6"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-part27-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup>
the
band
started
to
ponder
about
splitting
up
and
went
on
hiatus
after
a
promotional
tour
in
1990.
During
the
hiatus
the
band
members
formed
a
lighthearted
big-band
named
Hlj&oacute;msveit
Kondr&aacute;ds
B,
in
which
Bj&ouml;rk
played
<a
href="/wiki/Clarinet?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Clarinet">clarinet</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-secrethistory_12-7"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-secrethistory-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-part27_18-7"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-part27-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup>
It
was
during
the
hiatus
that
Bj&ouml;rk
started
working
on
her
solo
projects.
In
1990
she
provided
background
vocals
on
<i>Gums</i>,
an
album
by
a
band
called
Bless.<sup
id="cite_ref-secrethistory_12-8"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-secrethistory-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
the
same
year
the
singer
recorded
<i><a
href="/wiki/Gling-Gl%C3%B3?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Gling-Gl&oacute;">Gling-Gl&oacute;</a></i>,
a
collection
of
popular
<a
href="/wiki/Jazz?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jazz">jazz</a>
and
original
work,
with
the
jazz
group
<a
href="/wiki/Tr%C3%AD%C3%B3_Gu%C3%B0mundar_Ing%C3%B3lfssonar?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tr&iacute;&oacute;
Gu&eth;mundar
Ing&oacute;lfssonar">Tr&iacute;&oacute;
Gu&eth;mundar
Ing&oacute;lfssonar</a>,
which
is
her
best-selling
album
in
her
home
country
still
nowadays.<sup
id="cite_ref-saga_13-13"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-saga-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-part27_18-8"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-part27-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup>
Bj&ouml;rk
also
contributed
vocals
to
<a
href="/wiki/808_State?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="808
State">808
State</a>'s
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Ex:el?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ex:el">ex:el</a></i>,
with
whom
she
cultivated
her
interest
in
<a
href="/wiki/House_music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="House
music">house
music</a>.
She
contributed
vocals
on
the
songs
&quot;Qmart&quot;
and
on
&quot;Ooops&quot;,
which
was
released
as
a
single
in
the
UK
in
1991.<sup
id="cite_ref-secrethistory_12-9"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-secrethistory-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup>
She
also
contributed
vocals
to
the
song
&quot;Falling&quot;,
on
the
album
<i>Island</i>
by
<a
href="/wiki/Current_93?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Current
93">Current
93</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Hilmar_%C3%96rn_Hilmarsson?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hilmar
&Ouml;rn
Hilmarsson">Hilmar
&Ouml;rn
Hilmarsson</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-secrethistory_12-10"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-secrethistory-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
the
same
year
she
met
<a
href="/wiki/Harpist?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Harpist"
class="mw-redirect">harpist</a>
<a
href="/wiki/Corky_Hale?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Corky
Hale">Corky
Hale</a>,
with
whom
she
had
a
recording
session
that
was
bound
to
end
up
on
her
d&eacute;but
album.<sup
id="cite_ref-saga_13-14"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-saga-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>At
this
point,
Bj&ouml;rk
had
decided
to
leave
the
band
to
pursue
her
solo
career,
but
their
contract
included
the
making
of
one
last
album
with
a
subsequent
promotional
tour,
which
Bj&ouml;rk
agreed
to
do.<sup
id="cite_ref-part27_18-9"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-part27-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup>
<i><a
href="/wiki/Stick_Around_for_Joy?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Stick
Around
for
Joy">Stick
Around
for
Joy</a></i>
was
released
in
February
1992.
The
record
received
positive
reviews.
The
Sugarcubes
opened
for
<a
href="/wiki/U2?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="U2">U2</a>
during
their
<a
href="/wiki/Zoo_TV_Tour?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Zoo
TV
Tour">Zoo
TV
Tour</a>
in
October
and
November
1992,
playing
to
a
grand
total
of
700,000
people.<sup
id="cite_ref-part27_18-10"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-part27-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup>
Coinciding
with
this
string
of
concert,
their
label
released
a
<a
href="/wiki/Remix_album?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Remix
album">remix
album</a>
named
<i><a
href="/wiki/It%27s-It?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="It's-It">It's-It</a></i>.
Bj&ouml;rk
was
featured
on
two
tracks
of
the
soundtrack
for
the
1992
film
<i><a
href="/wiki/Remote_Control_(1992_film)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Remote
Control
(1992
film)">Remote
Control</a></i>
(known
as
<i>S&oacute;d&oacute;ma
Reykjav&iacute;k</i>
in
Iceland).<sup
id="cite_ref-secrethistory_12-11"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-secrethistory-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup>
After
the
Sugarcubes
played
one
last
gig
at
the
Reykjav&iacute;k
club
Tungli&eth;
around
Christmas,
they
decided
to
split
up.<sup
id="cite_ref-part27_18-11"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-part27-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup>
They
are
nowadays
recognized
as
&quot;Iceland's
biggest
rock
band&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-19"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="1992.E2.80.9396:_Debut_and_Post">1992–96:
<i>Debut</i>
and
<i>Post</i></span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Bj%C3%B6rk&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4"
title="Edit
section:
1992–96:
Debut
and
Post">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>In
1993,
the
Sugarcubes
split
up.
They
remain
friends
and
are
all
still
involved
in
the
management
of
Smekkleysa/Bad
Taste.
Bj&ouml;rk
moved
to
<a
href="/wiki/London?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="London">London</a>
to
pursue
a
solo
career;
she
began
working
with
producer
<a
href="/wiki/Nellee_Hooper?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Nellee
Hooper">Nellee
Hooper</a>
(who
had
produced
for
<a
href="/wiki/Massive_Attack?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Massive
Attack">Massive
Attack</a>,
among
others).
Their
partnership
produced
Bj&ouml;rk's
first
international
solo
hit,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Human_Behaviour?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Human
Behaviour">Human
Behaviour</a>&quot;,
a
clattering
dance
track
based
on
a
guitar
rhythm
sampled
from
<a
href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B4nio_Carlos_Jobim?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ant&ocirc;nio
Carlos
Jobim">Ant&ocirc;nio
Carlos
Jobim</a>.
In
most
countries,
the
song
was
not
widely
played
on
radio
but
was
widely
seen
on
MTV,
accompanied
by
an
influential
video
by
Oscar-winning
film
director
<a
href="/wiki/Michel_Gondry?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Michel
Gondry">Michel
Gondry</a>,
who
would
become
a
frequent
collaborator
for
Bj&ouml;rk.<sup
id="cite_ref-20"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Her
solo
debut
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Debut_(Bj%C3%B6rk_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Debut
(Bj&ouml;rk
album)">Debut</a></i>,
was
released
in
June
1993
to
positive
reviews;
it
was
named
album
of
the
year
by
<i><a
href="/wiki/NME?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="NME">NME</a></i>
and
eventually
went
<a
href="/wiki/Platinum_album?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Platinum
album"
class="mw-redirect">platinum</a>
in
the
United
States.<sup
id="cite_ref-RIAA_21-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-RIAA-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup>
<i>Debut</i>
was
the
leap
Bj&ouml;rk
made
from
being
in
numerous
bands
during
her
teens
and
early
twenties
to
her
solo
career.
But
although
this
was
far
from
her
real
debut
as
a
singer
and
musician,
having
released
her
first
solo
album
at
the
age
of
11,
she
named
the
album
<i>Debut</i>
to
signify
a
start
of
something
brand
new.
<i>Debut</i>
had
a
mix
of
songs
Bj&ouml;rk
had
been
writing
since
she
was
a
teenager,
as
well
as
more
recent
lyrical
collaborations
with
Hooper.
Although
the
music
was
mostly
dance-oriented,
it
was
varied
in
instrumentation.
One
single
from
the
album,
&quot;Venus
as
a
Boy&quot;,
featured
a
<a
href="/wiki/Bollywood?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bollywood">Bollywood</a>-influenced
string
arrangement.
Bj&ouml;rk
covered
the
jazz
standard
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Like_Someone_in_Love?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Like
Someone
in
Love">Like
Someone
in
Love</a>&quot;
to
the
accompaniment
of
a
harp,
and
the
final
track,
&quot;The
Anchor
Song&quot;,
was
sung
with
only
a
saxophone
ensemble
for
accompaniment.</p>








<p>At
the
1994
<a
href="/wiki/BRIT_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="BRIT
Awards"
class="mw-redirect">BRIT
Awards</a>,
Bj&ouml;rk
won
the
awards
for
Best
International
Female
and
Best
International
Newcomer.<sup
id="cite_ref-22"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
success
of
<i>Debut</i>
enabled
her
to
collaborate
with
British
and
other
artists
on
one-off
tracks.
She
worked
with
<a
href="/wiki/David_Arnold?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="David
Arnold">David
Arnold</a>
on
<a
href="/wiki/Play_Dead_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Play
Dead
(song)">&quot;Play
Dead&quot;</a>,
the
theme
to
the
1993
film
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Young_Americans_(film)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Young
Americans
(film)">The
Young
Americans</a></i>
(which
appeared
as
a
bonus
track
on
a
re-release
of
<i>Debut</i>),
collaborated
on
two
songs
for
<a
href="/wiki/Tricky_(musician)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tricky
(musician)">Tricky</a>'s
<i><a
href="/wiki/Nearly_God?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Nearly
God">Nearly
God</a></i>
project,
appeared
on
a
track
on
the
1997
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Not_for_Threes?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Not
for
Threes">Not
for
Threes</a></i>
by
<a
href="/wiki/Plaid_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Plaid
(band)">Plaid</a>
(which
was
released
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/Warp_(record_label)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Warp
(record
label)">Warp
Records</a>
label),
and
co-wrote
the
song
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Bedtime_Story_(Madonna_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bedtime
Story
(Madonna
song)">Bedtime
Story</a>&quot;
for
<a
href="/wiki/Madonna_(entertainer)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Madonna
(entertainer)">Madonna</a>'s
1994
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Bedtime_Stories_(Madonna_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bedtime
Stories
(Madonna
album)">Bedtime
Stories</a></i>.</p>








<p><i><a
href="/wiki/Post_(Bj%C3%B6rk_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Post
(Bj&ouml;rk
album)">Post</a></i>
was
Bj&ouml;rk's
second
solo
studio
album.
Released
in
June
1995,
the
album
was
produced
in
conjunction
with
<a
href="/wiki/Nellee_Hooper?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Nellee
Hooper">Nellee
Hooper</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Tricky_(musician)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tricky
(musician)">Tricky</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Graham_Massey?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Graham
Massey">Graham
Massey</a>
of
<a
href="/wiki/808_State?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="808
State">808
State</a>,
and
electronica
producer
<a
href="/wiki/Howie_B?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Howie
B">Howie
B</a>.
Building
on
the
success
of
<i>Debut</i>,
Bj&ouml;rk
continued
to
pursue
different
sounds,
taking
particular
interest
in
<a
href="/wiki/Dance_music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Dance
music">dance</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Techno?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Techno">techno</a>.
Production
by
Tricky
and
Howie
B
also
provided
trip
hop/electronica-like
sounds
on
tracks
like
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Possibly_Maybe?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Possibly
Maybe">Possibly
Maybe</a>&quot;
and
&quot;Enjoy&quot;.
It
was
these
producers'
influence
along
with
older
friend
Graham
Massey
that
inspired
Bj&ouml;rk
to
create
material
like
the
storming
<a
href="/wiki/Industrial_music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Industrial
music">industrial</a>
beats
of
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Army_of_Me_(Bj%C3%B6rk_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Army
of
Me
(Bj&ouml;rk
song)">Army
of
Me</a>&quot;.
<i>Post</i>
however
also
included
more
subtle
and
playful
moments
than
<i>Debut</i>,
with
deeper
jazz
and
orchestral
arrangements
on
some
tracks
and
a
mood
of
intimate
contemplation
toward
the
end.</p>








<p>The
album
was
ranked
number
7
in
<i><a
href="/wiki/Spin_(magazine)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Spin
(magazine)">Spin</a>'</i>s
&quot;Top
90
Albums
of
the
'90s&quot;
list
and
number
75
in
its
&quot;100
Greatest
Albums,
1985–2005&quot;
list.<sup
id="cite_ref-23"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-24"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup>
<i>Post</i>
and
<i><a
href="/wiki/Homogenic?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Homogenic">Homogenic</a></i>
were
placed
back
to
back
on
<a
href="/wiki/Pitchfork_Media?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pitchfork
Media">Pitchfork
Media</a>'s
&quot;Top
Albums
of
the
'90s&quot;
list
at
numbers
21
and
20,
respectively.<sup
id="cite_ref-25"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-26"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
2003,
the
album
was
ranked
number
373
on
<i><a
href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rolling
Stone">Rolling
Stone</a></i>
magazine's
list
of
<a
href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone%27s_500_Greatest_Albums_of_All_Time?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rolling
Stone's
500
Greatest
Albums
of
All
Time">the
500
greatest
albums
of
all
time</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-27"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Although
again
Bj&ouml;rk
received
more
mainstream
attention
for
her
videos
than
her
singles,
<i>Post</i>
included
several
UK
pop
hits
and
was
eventually
certified
<a
href="/wiki/RIAA_certification?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="RIAA
certification">platinum</a>
in
the
US.<sup
id="cite_ref-RIAA_21-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-RIAA-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup>
Bj&ouml;rk
also
contributed
to
the
1995
<a
href="/wiki/Hector_Zazou?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hector
Zazou">Hector
Zazou</a>
collaborative
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Chansons_des_mers_froides?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Chansons
des
mers
froides">Chansons
des
mers
froides</a></i>,
singing
the
traditional
Icelandic
song
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/V%C3%ADsur_Vatnsenda-R%C3%B3su?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="V&iacute;sur
Vatnsenda-R&oacute;su">V&iacute;sur
Vatnsenda-R&oacute;su</a>&quot;.</p>

class="mw-headline"

beats,
strings,

and
<i>Vespertine</i></span>

and

1998

<p>In
1997,
the
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Homogenic?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Homogenic">Homogenic</a></i>
was
released.
It
marked
a
dramatic
shift
from
her
earlier
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Pixie?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pixie">pixie</a>&quot;
image
cultivated
on
the
<i>Debut</i>
and
<i>Post</i>
albums.
Bj&ouml;rk
worked
with
producers
<a
href="/wiki/Mark_Bell_(British_musician)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mark
Bell
(British
musician)">Mark
Bell</a>
of
<a
href="/wiki/LFO_(British_band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="LFO
(British
band)">LFO</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Howie_B?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Howie
B">Howie
B</a>
on
the
album,
as
well
as
<a
href="/wiki/Eumir_Deodato?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Eumir
Deodato">Eumir
Deodato</a>;
numerous
remixes
followed.
<i>Homogenic</i>
was
her
first
conceptually
self-contained
album
and
is
regarded
as
one
of
Bj&ouml;rk's
most
experimental
and
extroverted
works
to
date,
with
enormous
beats
that
reflect
the
landscape
of
Iceland,
most
notably
in
the
song
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/J%C3%B3ga?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="J&oacute;ga">J&oacute;ga</a>&quot;,
which
fuses
lush
strings
with
rocky
electronic
crunches.
The
album
was
certified
<a
href="/wiki/RIAA_certification?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="RIAA
certification">gold</a>
in
the
US
in
2001.<sup
id="cite_ref-RIAA_21-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-RIAA-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>The
emotionally
charged
album
contains
a
string
of
<a
href="/wiki/Music_video?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Music
video">music
videos</a>,
several
of
which
received
airplay
on
<a
href="/wiki/MTV?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="MTV">MTV</a>.
The
video
for
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Bachelorette_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bachelorette
(song)">Bachelorette</a>&quot;
was
directed
by
frequent
collaborator
<a
href="/wiki/Michel_Gondry?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Michel
Gondry">Michel
Gondry</a>,
while
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/All_Is_Full_of_Love?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="All
Is
Full
of
Love">All
Is
Full
of
Love</a>&quot;
was
directed
by
<a
href="/wiki/Chris_Cunningham?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Chris
Cunningham">Chris
Cunningham</a>.
The
single
&quot;All
is
Full
of
Love&quot;
was
also
the
first
<a
href="/wiki/DVD?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="DVD">DVD</a>
single
to
ever
be
released
in
the
US,
which
paved
the
way
for
other
artists
to
include
DVD
video
and
other
<a
href="/wiki/Multimedia?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Multimedia">multimedia</a>
features
with
their
singles.</p>








<p>In
an
interview
with
<i><a
href="/wiki/Spin_(magazine)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Spin
(magazine)">Spin</a></i>
magazine,
<a
href="/wiki/Radiohead?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Radiohead">Radiohead</a>
singer
<a
href="/wiki/Thom_Yorke?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Thom
Yorke">Thom
Yorke</a>
called
the
song
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Unravel?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Unravel">Unravel</a>&quot;
from
this
album
his
favourite
song
ever,
claiming
&quot;I'm
trying
to
get
Radiohead
to
do
a
cover
because
I
think
it's
one
of
the
most
beautiful
songs
I've
ever
heard.&quot;
In
November
2007,
the
band
covered
the
song
as
part
of
a
live
webcast.<sup
id="cite_ref-28"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<div
class="thumb
tright">









<div
class="thumbinner"
style="width:222px;">









<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Bj%C3%B6rk2001.jpg"

/></a>

<div

<a

src="http://sp.ask.com/sh/i/wiki/magnify-clip.png"

alt=""
/></a>










</div>
Bj&ouml;rk
performing
at
the











<a
href="/wiki/Radio_City_Music_Hall?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Radio
City
Music
Hall">Radio
City
Music
Hall</a>
in
2001









</div>









</div>

<p>In
2001,
Bj&ouml;rk
released
the
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Vespertine?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Vespertine">Vespertine</a></i>.
The
album
featured
chamber
orchestras,
choirs,
hushed
vocals,
microbeats
made
from
household
sounds,
and
personal,
vulnerable
themes.
She
collaborated
with
experimental
sound
manipulators
<a
href="/wiki/Matmos?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Matmos">Matmos</a>,
Denmark-based
<a
href="/wiki/Thomas_Knak?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Thomas
Knak">DJ
Thomas
Knak</a>,
and
the
experimental
<a
href="/wiki/Harp?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Harp">harpist</a>
<a
href="/wiki/Zeena_Parkins?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Zeena
Parkins">Zeena
Parkins</a>
for
the
album.
Lyrical
sources
included
the
works
of
American
<a
href="/wiki/Poetry?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Poetry">poet</a>
<a
href="/wiki/E._E._Cummings?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="E.
E.
Cummings">E.
E.
Cummings</a>,
the
American
independent
filmmaker
<a
href="/wiki/Harmony_Korine?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Harmony
Korine">Harmony
Korine</a>,
and
English
playwright
<a
href="/wiki/Sarah_Kane?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sarah
Kane">Sarah
Kane</a>'s
penultimate
play,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Crave_(play)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Crave
(play)">Crave</a></i>.
To
coincide
with
the
album's
release,
Bj&ouml;rk
released
a
<a
href="/wiki/Coffee_table_book?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Coffee
table
book">coffee
table
book</a>
of
loose
prose
and
photographs
titled
<i><a
href="/wiki/Bj%C3%B6rk_(book)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bj&ouml;rk
(book)">Bj&ouml;rk</a></i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-29"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup>
Bj&ouml;rk
embarked
on
a
tour
of
theatres
and
opera
houses
in
Europe
and
North
America
in
support
of
the
album,
accompanied
by
the
musicians
Matmos
and
Zeena
Parkins
and
an
<a
href="/wiki/Inuit?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Inuit">Inuit</a>
choir,
whom
she
had
held
auditions
for
on
a
trip
to
Greenland
prior
to
the
tour.<sup
id="cite_ref-30"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup>
At
the
time,
<i>Vespertine</i>
was
Bj&ouml;rk's
quickest
selling
album
ever,
having
sold
two
million
copies
by
the
end
of
2001.<sup
id="cite_ref-31"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p><i>Vespertine</i>
spawned
three
singles:
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Hidden_Place?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hidden
Place">Hidden
Place</a>&quot;,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Pagan_Poetry?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pagan
Poetry">Pagan
Poetry</a>&quot;,
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Cocoon_(Bj%C3%B6rk_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Cocoon
(Bj&ouml;rk
song)">Cocoon</a>&quot;.
<a
href="/wiki/MTV2?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="MTV2">MTV2</a>
played
the
album's
first
video,
&quot;Hidden
Place&quot;,
which
was
subsequently
released
as
a
DVD
single.
However,
the
next
video,
for
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Pagan_Poetry?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pagan
Poetry">Pagan
Poetry</a>&quot;,
brought
Bj&ouml;rk
to
an
even
higher
level
of
controversy
with
the
channel.
The
song's
video
features
graphic
piercings,
Bj&ouml;rk's
exposed
nipples,
and
simulated
<a
href="/wiki/Fellatio?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Fellatio">fellatio</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-32"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup>
As
a
result,
the
clip
was
initially
rarely
shown
by
MTV,
and
certain
parts
(for
example,
Bj&ouml;rk's
breasts)
were
<a
href="/wiki/Censorship?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Censorship">censored</a>
during
the
rare
occasions
when
it
was
played.
In
2002,
the
clip
finally
enjoyed
unedited
American
airing
as
part
of
a
late
night
special
on
MTV2
titled,
&quot;Most
Controversial
Music
Videos&quot;.
The
video
for
&quot;Cocoon&quot;
also
featured
a
seemingly
naked
Bj&ouml;rk
(actually
wearing
a
close
fitting
bodysuit),
this
time
with
her
nipples
secreting
a
red
thread
that
eventually
enveloped
the
singer
in
a
cocoon.
The
video
was
directed
by
Japanese
artist
<a
href="/wiki/Eiko_Ishioka?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Eiko
Ishioka">Eiko
Ishioka</a>
and
was
not
aired
by
<a
href="/wiki/MTV?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="MTV">MTV</a>.</p>








<p>The
year
2002
saw
the
appearance
of
the
CD
box
set
<i><a
href="/wiki/Family_Tree_(Bj%C3%B6rk_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Family
Tree
(Bj&ouml;rk
album)">Family
Tree</a></i>
containing
a
retrospective
of
Bj&ouml;rk's
career,
comprising
many
previously
unreleased
versions
of
her
compositions,
including
her
work
with
the
<a
href="/wiki/Brodsky_Quartet?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Brodsky
Quartet">Brodsky
Quartet</a>.
Also
released
alongside
<i>Family
Tree</i>
was
the
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Greatest_Hits_(Bj%C3%B6rk_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Greatest
Hits
(Bj&ouml;rk
album)">Greatest
Hits</a></i>,
a
retrospective
of
the
previous
10
years
of
her
solo
career
as
deemed
by
the
public.
The
songs
on
the
album
were
chosen
by
Bj&ouml;rk's
fans
through
a
poll
on
her
website.
A
DVD
edition
of
the
CD
was
also
released.
It
contained
all
of
Bj&ouml;rk's
solo
music
videos
up
to
that
point.
The
new
single
from
the
set,
&quot;It's
in
Our
Hands&quot;
charted
in
the
UK
at
number
37.
The
video,
directed
by
<a
href="/wiki/Spike_Jonze?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Spike
Jonze">Spike
Jonze</a>,
features
a
heavily
pregnant
Bj&ouml;rk.</p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="2003.E2.80.9306:_Med.C3.BAlla_and_vocal_development">2003–06:
<i>Med&uacute;lla</i>
and
vocal
development</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Bj%C3%B6rk&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6"
title="Edit
section:
2003–06:
Med&uacute;lla
and
vocal
development">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<div
class="thumb
tright">









<div
class="thumbinner"
style="width:182px;">









<a
href="/wiki?title=Special:Upload&amp;wpDestFile=Bjork_Hurricane.jpg"
class="new"
title="File:Bjork
Hurricane.jpg">File:Bjork
Hurricane.jpg</a>










<div
class="thumbcaption">










Bj&ouml;rk
at
the











<a
href="/wiki/Hurricane_Festival?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hurricane
Festival">Hurricane
Festival</a>
on
June
21,
2003









</div>









</div>








</div>








<p>Bj&ouml;rk
and
the
Brodsky
Quartet
recorded
a
composition
written,
especially
for
her,
by
composer
<a
href="/wiki/John_Tavener?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="John
Tavener">John
Tavener</a>
called
&quot;Prayer
of
the
Heart&quot;
in
2001,
and
it
was
played
then
for
a
slide
show
presentation
in
2003
for
the
American
photographer,
<a
href="/wiki/Nan_Goldin?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Nan
Goldin">Nan
Goldin</a>.</p>








<p>In
2003,
Bj&ouml;rk
released
a
box
set
called
<i><a
href="/wiki/Live_Box?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Live
Box">Live
Box</a></i>,
consisting
of
four
CDs
containing
<a
href="/wiki/Concert?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Concert">live
recordings</a>
of
her
previous
albums
and
a
DVD
featuring
a
video
of
one
track
from
each
CD.
Each
of
the
four
CDs
was
later
released
separately
at
a
reduced
price.</p>








<p>In
August
2004,
Bj&ouml;rk
released
<i><a
href="/wiki/Med%C3%BAlla?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Med&uacute;lla">Med&uacute;lla</a></i>.
During
production,
Bj&ouml;rk
decided
the
album
would
work
best
as
an
entirely
vocal-based
album.
However,
this
initial
plan
didn't
materialize
exactly
that
way,
as
the
majority
of
the
sounds
on
the
album
are
indeed
created
by
vocalists
but
several
feature
prominent
basic
electronic
programming.
Bj&ouml;rk
used
the
vocal
skills
of
<a
href="/wiki/Inuit_throat_singing?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Inuit
throat
singing">throat
singer</a>
<a
href="/wiki/Tagaq?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tagaq">Tagaq</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hip
hop
music">hip
hop</a>
<a
href="/wiki/Beatboxing?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Beatboxing">beatboxer</a>
<a
href="/wiki/Rahzel?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rahzel">Rahzel</a>,
Japanese
beatboxer
<a
href="/wiki/Dokaka?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Dokaka">Dokaka</a>,
avant-rocker
<a
href="/wiki/Mike_Patton?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mike
Patton">Mike
Patton</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Soft_Machine?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Soft
Machine">Soft
Machine</a>
drummer/singer
<a
href="/wiki/Robert_Wyatt?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Robert
Wyatt">Robert
Wyatt</a>,
and
several
<a
href="/wiki/Choir?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Choir">choirs</a>.
She
again
appropriated
text
from
E.
E.
Cummings
for
the
song
&quot;Sonnets/Unrealities
XI&quot;.
At
the
time,
<i>Med&uacute;lla</i>
became
her
highest
charting
album
in
the
US,
debuting
at
number
14.
It
has
since
been
surpassed
by
<i><a
href="/wiki/Volta_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Volta
(album)">Volta</a></i>,
which
debuted
at
number
nine
in
the
US.</p>








<p>In
August
2004,
Bj&ouml;rk
performed
the
song
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Oceania_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Oceania
(song)">Oceania</a>&quot;
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/2004_Summer_Olympics_opening_ceremony?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="2004
Summer
Olympics
opening
ceremony">Opening
Ceremony</a>
of
the
<a
href="/wiki/2004_Summer_Olympics?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="2004
Summer
Olympics">2004
Summer
Olympics</a>
in
<a
href="/wiki/Athens?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Athens">Athens</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Greece?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Greece">Greece</a>.
As
she
sang,
her
dress
slowly
unfurled
to
reveal
a
10,000
square
foot
(900
m&sup2;)
map
of
the
world,
which
she
let
flow
over
all
of
the
Olympic
athletes.
The
song
&quot;Oceania&quot;
was
written
especially
for
the
occasion
and
features
the
talents
of
<a
href="/wiki/Shlomo_(beatboxing_artist)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Shlomo
(beatboxing
artist)">Shlomo</a>,
a
<a
href="/wiki/Leeds?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Leeds">Leeds</a>-based
<a
href="/wiki/Beatboxing?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Beatboxing">beatboxer</a>,
and
a
London
choir.
An
alternate
version
of
the
song
began
circulating
on
the
Internet
with
additional
vocals
by
<a
href="/wiki/Kelis?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Kelis">Kelis</a>.
It
originally
appeared
on
the
promotional
&quot;Oceania&quot;
single
released
to
radio
stations
and
later
became
available
to
the
public
as
a
<a
href="/wiki/A-side_and_B-side?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="A-side
and
B-side">B-side</a>
of
the
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Who_Is_It_(Bj%C3%B6rk_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Who
Is
It
(Bj&ouml;rk
song)">Who
Is
It</a>&quot;
single,
which
charted
at
number
26
in
the
UK.
This
was
followed
in
early
2005
by
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Triumph_of_a_Heart?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Triumph
of
a
Heart">Triumph
of
a
Heart</a>&quot;,
charting
at
number
31.</p>








<p>A
video
for
the
potential
next
single,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Where_Is_the_Line?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Where
Is
the
Line">Where
Is
the
Line</a>&quot;,
was
filmed
in
collaboration
with
the
Icelandic
artist
<a
href="/wiki/Gabr%C3%ADela_Fri%C3%B0riksd%C3%B3ttir?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Gabr&iacute;ela
Fri&eth;riksd&oacute;ttir">Gabr&iacute;ela
Fri&eth;riksd&oacute;ttir</a>
in
late
2004.
This
was
initially
a
sequence
from
an
art
installation
movie
of
the
artists
but
was
released
exclusively
on
the
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Med%C3%BAlla_Videos?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Med&uacute;lla
Videos">Med&uacute;lla
Videos</a></i>
DVD
as
an
official
promo
for
the
track.</p>

class="thumb
tleft">

style="width:227px;">
